A Tour of the National Children's Reading Material Exhibition: Courteous and Kind Reception, Children Reluctant to Put Down Books and Linger 177

(Nanjing Correspondence) As the National Children's Year begins, and compulsory education is being implemented, children's education is gradually gaining attention. The National Children's Reading Material Exhibition, sponsored by the National Children's Year Implementation Committee of the Ministry of Education, concluded yesterday (the 30th) at the Daxing Palace Elementary School. Our reporter made a special trip to visit it and records the following miscellaneous notes:

……

At the entrance of the venue, there is a "National Children's Year Sign," shaped like an inverted L, with the words in red artistic font, attracting the attention of passersby. After entering, one proceeds along the designated route. At the entrance, the eight large characters "Vigorously Implement Child-Centered Education" are written. Then, one arrives at the signing area to sign in. Here, visitor instructions and a list of exhibited book categories are displayed. Afterward, one enters the first exhibition room, which features supplementary reading materials, divided into categories such as Nature, Society, Literature, Series, and Periodicals. Part of it is children's supplementary reading material compiled and printed by local elementary schools themselves. Another part is children's publications from Commercial Press, Zhonghua Book Company, The World Book Company, Datong Book Company, and publications for the Children's Year. This type of book is particularly abundant, displayed in a total of three rooms. According to the visitor rules, visitors can freely pick up and read the books. Therefore, at this time, there are many children, mostly eleven or twelve years old, some only eight or nine years old, flipping through them non-stop. Some are quietly reciting, revealing a spirit of self-motivated learning. It turns out that schools are currently on winter vacation. The exhibition had designated February 1st and the 3rd and 4th as visiting days for students, but these elementary school students are taking advantage of the holiday to visit early, which is truly commendable.

……

In the second exhibition room, a large silk banner with black characters on a red background hangs, the original text being "Girls and boys must receive education equally." On the surrounding walls, many wooden signs are also hung, with many cautionary statements written on them, transcribed as follows: (1) Children's books are a treasure trove of children's knowledge; (2) Parents should choose and purchase excellent reading materials for their children; (3) Elementary schools should provide more reading materials for children to read; (4) Children should save their candy money to buy reading materials; (5) The habit of reading should be cultivated from a young age; (6) The most important conditions for choosing reading materials are that they are interesting, meaningful, and suitable for their level.

……

The exhibition rooms were originally classrooms of the Daxing Palace Elementary School, so the capacity is not very large. When the reporter entered the third exhibition room, it was almost overcrowded. The reporter immediately took a count, finding a total of forty-two people, including eighteen adults and twenty-four children, with more children than adults. This is probably a rare phenomenon in any exhibition. What is particularly worth mentioning is that most of the adult visitors were just taking a quick look and rarely browsing carefully, while the children, on the other hand, were reluctant to put down the books and seemed to linger indefinitely. The reporter lingered in this room for about ten minutes, and only three or five children left, while the adults had already changed to another group. This clearly demonstrates how interested children are in the exhibition.

……

In each exhibition room, the reception duties are all handled by children, which is precisely giving them an opportunity to show their work. At this time, an adult visitor was eating melon seeds when a female receptionist, about thirteen or fourteen years old, noticed and walked up to him, saying kindly, "Please don't eat anything in the exhibition hall." The person certainly accepted, but the reporter felt ashamed for the general adult population, because this is an embarrassing thing for adults in front of children.

……

The fourth exhibition room features textbooks, divided into subjects such as Chinese, Music, Hygiene, General Knowledge, Art, and Handicraft. On the wall hangs a red silk banner with "New Children Create New China," which is very bright and eye-catching. Here are displayed many elementary school textbooks that are no longer in use. The reporter casually reviewed a few volumes. One is a higher elementary school moral cultivation textbook, published by the Compilation and Translation Bureau of the Ministry of Education in December of the second year of the Xuantong era, compiled by Chen Xugong and others. Another is a single-grade elementary school moral cultivation teaching material, published by the China Book Company in April of the second year of the Xuantong era, compiled by Jin ..., Gu Zhuo, Gu Zuji, and others. Because of the reporter's age, I had never read these two books, so seeing this type of book, I felt particularly interested. It is estimated that those who read textbooks from this period should be at least thirty-five years old.

……

The fifth and sixth exhibition rooms contain reference books. Part of them are children's books from various countries around the world, collected by the committee submitting a request to the Ministry of Education to forward to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, instructing embassies abroad to collect them from the educational institutions of the countries where they are stationed. There are about ten types each from eleven countries including England, America, Germany, Italy, France, Japan, Austria, Netherlands, Soviet Union, Poland, and Denmark, which are quite precious.

……

The seventh exhibition room contains popular children's reading materials from society, which are the generally poor children's reading materials sold on door panels and book stalls, the so-called "comic strips," such as "Hun Yuan Mirror," "Red-Clad Thief," "Feng Niang," "Trouble at the Dragon Boat Race," "Lord Wu's Private Visit to Nine Human Heads," "Qin Xianglian Bringing Her Child to Find Her Husband, Chen Shimei Denying His Former Wife," etc. There are a total of 229 types. What exactly is the impact of this type of reading material on general underage children? This is really a question that needs attention.

……

The books displayed this time are divided into three major categories: supplementary reading materials, textbooks, and reference books, further divided into eighteen groups, 2,450 types, and 12,4858 volumes. Among them are letterpress editions, lithographic editions, woodcut editions, with illustrations, five-color lithographs, textbooks, reference books, after-school supplementary reading materials, children's books from various countries, single-volume books, series, journals, periodicals, etc., truly a great variety, a magnificent spectacle.

……

On the eve of the opening of the children's book exhibition, the National Children's Year Implementation Committee announced the purpose of holding the exhibition to society. In essence, there are about the following points: (1) To provide a general overview for the Chinese people to correct their perceptions of children's books; (2) To provide research for experts to improve and select children's books; (3) To provide a reference for the literary world, hoping that both new and old writers will devote more effort to compiling and writing children's books. In addition, it is hoped that the publishing industry will solicit more manuscripts in the future and improve printing and binding, so that children's books can be refined and improved, in order to benefit children.

……

The exhibition is scheduled to run from January 30th to February 5th. After the closing, it is planned to be transported to major cities across the country for a roving exhibition, to arouse the attention of adults and children nationwide. (1.31.1 Fan)

Convener Yan Fuxui, (3) Essay Group Zhuang Zeyi, Tai Shuangqiu, Chen Jianxiao, Wu Junsheng, Xie Xunchu, Convener Zhuang Zeyi, (4) Proposal Group Huang Pu, Gao Han, Jiang Qi, Lu Chunrong, Chen Lijiang, Liu Naijing, Zheng Zonghai, Zhang Huai, Convener Huang Pu, (5) Documentation Group Hu Yi, Luo Lun, Zhang Anguo, Convener Hu Yi, (6) Reception Group Beijing Li Jianxun, Liu Jianfang, Nanjing Chang Daozhi, Ai Wei, Shanghai Tai Shuangqiu, Zheng Tonghe, Tianjin Qi Guoliang, Guangdong Cui Zaiyang, Wuxi Gao Yang, Anqing Hao Yaodong, Hunan Du Yuanzai, Wuhan Jiang Qi, Hangzhou Zhuang Zeyi, Kaifeng Li Buqing, Xiamen Sun Guiding, Fuzhou Lin Jingrun,

Glimpses of Proposals: It is said that the annual meeting received over forty proposals, the important ones being: (1) Inviting various social science societies to jointly hold an annual meeting next year; (2) The conference organizing a special period education research committee to discuss education policies and implementation plans during the current national crisis, for the reference of education administrative authorities; (3) Suggesting that future education policies should pay attention to physical fitness and spiritual training, correcting the past emphasis on imparting book knowledge; (4) Requesting the Ministry of Education to strictly prohibit the revision of textbooks; (5) The highest goal of civil education facilities should be to organize the masses and cultivate the strength of mass groups; (6) Civil education institutions should pay special attention to teaching by district division, seeking in-depth understanding; (7) Teacher training should also emphasize civil education practical talents; (8) Requesting the Academia Sinica to quickly establish an education research institute; (9) Requesting attention to the use of Sino-French and Sino-Belgian Boxer Indemnity funds; (10) Suggesting submitting a request to the Ministry of Education to order all provinces to restore education bureaus; (11) The association cooperating with local governments to establish education experimental zones; (12) Coordinating the preparation and printing of in-service training books and newspapers for primary and secondary school teachers nationwide; (13) Preparing for and setting a deadline for the establishment of an education museum; (14) Requesting the Ministry of Education to revise the elementary school regulations.

Board Meeting: The board members of the association are Liu Jianfang, Zhuang Zeyi, Guan Tonghe, Zheng Zonghai, Chen Lijiang, Yang Lianggong, Xu Keshi, Tai Shuangqiu, Chen Jianxiao, Chang Daozhi, Zhang Boling, Ou Yuanhuai, Tao Zhihang, Meng Xiancheng, Du Zuozhou. The alternate board members are Xie Xunchu, Ai Wei, Cheng Qibao, Chen Heqin, Guo Yicen. The standing board members are Chen Jianxiao, Xu Keshi, Yang Lianggong, Zheng Tonghe, Chen Lijiang. A board meeting was held on the 31st to determine the focus of discussion for this year's annual meeting and to appoint Xu Keshi, Liu Jianfang, Chen Shi, Zheng Xigu, Zhu Jingnong, Tai Shuangqiu, and Cheng Qibao as the presidium of the conference.

Tour Locations: The tour locations for members outside the meeting have also been pre-arranged, including Yellow Crane Tower in Wuchang, Shouyi Park, Chen Youliang's Tomb, Baobing Hall, Hongshan, Zhuodaoquan, Luojia Mountain, Wuhan University, East Lake, Haiguang Agricultural Garden, Provincial Education College, Zhongshan Park in Hankou, Broadcasting Station, Water Plant, Power Plant, Boyatai in Hanyang, Qingchuan Pavilion, Guiyuan Temple, Arsenal, Parrot Island Erheng Tomb, Lingshan Mountain in the suburbs of Wuchang, Tomb of the King of Chu, Jiufeng Mountain, Yingcheng Hot Springs, and Jigong Mountain on the border of Hubei and Henan.

Children's Educational Novel: Little Men (1)(6)(5) Original work by Louisa M. Alcott, translated by Zheng Xiaocang

Dan fell safely; but the bough, suddenly relieved of half its weight, flew as suddenly upward, sending Don, who was performing a somersault in his haste to alight first, off his balance, so that he tumbled down in a heap.

“It’s nothing; I shall be all right in a minute,” he said, as he sat up, rather pale, and a little dizzy, while the lads gathered round him with wondering admiration.

“You are a brick, Don, and I’m awfully obliged,” said Nat.

“It wasn’t anything,” muttered Don, slowly scrambling up.

“I say it was a jolly good thing to do, and I’ll shake hands, though you are –” Nat stopped the unlucky word on his tongue, and held out his hand, feeling himself uncommonly magnanimous.

“I don’t care to shake hands with a sneak;” said Don, giving him a withering glance as he spoke, and Nat, remembering the wash, retreated in haste.

“Come, old fellow; let me help you along;” and Ned walked him away, leaving the others to discuss Don and to declare that ‘the old fellow had better burn that infernal money, than have such a row about it.’

Chinese Football League: Guangdong Wins Group B Cup Championship: Yesterday's Final, Three to Zero Victory Over Yousheng 186

Eight teams joined the competition for the Chinese Football Association Group B Cup, and after several eliminations, Guangdong and Yousheng teams won the final rights. The two teams played against each other at Shen Garden at 10:00 AM yesterday to determine who would win the championship. In the first half, the offense and defense were evenly matched, and each had little development. It was not until about six or seven minutes before the end that Yousheng's defense was slightly lacking, and Lin Guoyong of Guangdong headed in a goal. Because Guangdong's rear defense was tight, Yousheng had no chance to take advantage, and instead Zhao Jie and Zhang Ziquan attacked the goal one after another. 32nd Army Boxing Team to Compete with Westerners Tomorrow 188

The 32nd Army Boxing Team, a group of four people, led by Zhao Yunxie, director of the military sports department, arrived in Shanghai a few days ago and stayed at the Delin Apartment. In recent days, they have been going to the gymnasium of the Western Youth Association on Jing'an Temple Road to practice, and have received instructions from boxing professor Ding Geer of the association, which has been quite rewarding. The team is scheduled to compete with Shanghai Western amateur boxers at 6:00 PM tomorrow. According to the team leader Zhao, this trip to Shanghai was initiated by Western expatriates in Shanghai who wanted to sponsor Chinese boxers to attend the World Amateur Boxing Championships held in Chicago, and the invitation was forwarded by Shen Siliang, secretary general of the Sports Association.

Economic Special

The Process of Solving the Soviet Grain Problem 191

— Wu Binglian

——From the Implementation to the Abolition of the Bread Rationing System

Following the October Revolution, Russia's domestic production was at a standstill due to the impact of years of war, and the national economy was almost completely bankrupt. Coupled with the economic blockade and military encirclement by international imperialism, the Soviet Union faced an extremely serious grain problem. During this period, famine was almost universal throughout the Soviet Union. It was not until the implementation of the New Economic Policy that the Soviet proletariat was able to escape from extreme hunger and thirst. However, the grain problem remained very serious in the Soviet Union.

With the commencement of the First Five-Year Plan, the Soviet government formally established a bread rationing system to ensure the supply of grain to industrial centers and agricultural areas. When this system began to be implemented, the Soviet Union had already overcome the chaos, instability, and famine of the early days, and the national economy gradually stabilized. However, the number of collective farms and Soviet farms in the country was still small. Although the system of private land ownership had been abolished, the wealthy peasants had not been completely eliminated. Agricultural technology lagged behind industrial technology, and yields were low, giving the independent small-scale peasant economy an advantage. Therefore, under these circumstances, the Soviet government had to adopt the bread rationing system to ensure the policy and speed of industrialization, improve the backwardness of agriculture, and promote the economic interests and technological development of rural areas. They feared that the backwardness of small-scale peasant agriculture would affect industrial development. Therefore, they had to consider the grain supply to workers, cities, and raw material production areas for light industry.

At the end of 1928 and the beginning of 1929, as soon as the bread rationing system was implemented, the Soviet government immediately concentrated 650 million poods (one pood equals 36.11 pounds) of grain, controlled the grain market to prevent grain speculation, and used state-organized grain supply to control grain distribution. The government set fixed prices and distributed grain to workers in industrial raw material production areas and industrial centers.

This system was first implemented in Leningrad and Moscow, and then gradually spread to other regions. At that time, the implementation of this system caused wavering among the right-wing and "left-wing" elements within the Soviet Communist Party. They opposed attacking the remnants of capitalism and opposed collectivization in the countryside. However, the Soviet government overcame their fallacies and resolutely implemented this decision until the victory of socialist construction was achieved.

After the implementation of the bread rationing system in 1928, the state grain reserves in the Soviet Union increased year by year. By 1934, the grain reserves under state control had reached 1.5 billion poods, an increase of about 2.5 times compared to 1928. Moreover, the sources of grain reserves also underwent significant changes during these years. In 1929, 86 percent of the stored grain came from independent farmers, while collective farms accounted for only 14 percent. This means that the small-scale peasant economy still held a significant advantage in 1929. However, in 1934, the situation was very different, or rather, it was the opposite of 1929: collective farms and state-owned farms accounted for 92 percent of the stored grain in that year, while independent farmers accounted for only 8 percent. This demonstrates the significant victory of collectivization in the countryside.

The number of people receiving centralized grain supply, in other words, the number of people eligible for bread ration coupons, also increased year by year. In terms of the urban population alone, it had increased by 14.3 million between 1930 and 1934. In 1930, only 16 million urban workers had bread ration coupons, while in 1934, the number had reached 40.3 million, including 1.07 million with special coupons, 11.8 million with Class A coupons, 9.6 million with Class B coupons, and 8.6 million with Class C coupons. Among these four types of coupons, special coupons and Class A coupons enjoyed priority in supply.

People who had bread ration coupons could collect their grain according to the amount specified on the coupons at that time. Otherwise, they could only buy from state-owned stores, but the price of this free purchase method was several times higher than the state-set price. According to statistics from 1930, out of the 154 million people in the Soviet Union, 64.3 million had bread ration coupons, while the remaining 90.7 million had to buy grain from state-owned stores. At that time, the eligibility for bread ration coupons was generally stipulated as follows:

Workers participating in socialist construction, whether laborers in factories or farms.

Staff of government agencies and stores, and students in schools.

Family members of laborers, and those whose health was harmed due to state affairs—the disabled.

In other words, those who did not participate in socialist construction did not have the right to receive grain supply in the Soviet Union. On the contrary, the more workers strived to engage in socialist construction, the more preferential treatment they received. The government set fixed prices for the most hardworking workers, allowing them to enjoy the most privileged rights because the price of private grain was very high at that time, sometimes even exceeding the state-set price by more than 40 times.

For those who did not have bread ration coupons, the system was naturally very inconvenient for them. However, the Soviet government had to do so in order to implement their plans. The only way to remedy this inconvenience at that time was to expand the development of state-owned stores and cooperatives and eliminate private commerce. At the same time, efforts were made to increase the source of grain (production) year by year to ensure the grain supply, and then restore normal operations. The Central Executive Committee and the People's Committee of the Soviet Union repeatedly discussed this point, which is why they decided to abolish the bread rationing system in November 1934. This decision was not accidental, just as the implementation of the bread rationing system in 1928 had its inevitable factors.

First, there was a large increase in state-owned stores and cooperatives and a rapid elimination of private commerce during these years. This is reflected in the following figures:——

(Total number of state-owned stores and cooperatives)

1928 123,000

1934 283,000

In 1928, there were still 215,000 private stores, accounting for 63% of all commerce. However, by 1934, they had all been eliminated. Therefore, the development of state commerce replaced private commerce, which also determined the trend of abolishing the bread rationing system.

Molotov said in the report on the abolition of the bread rationing system: "The development of commerce is of great significance for the abolition of the bread rationing system. Therefore, we will pay special attention to it... Retail commerce has greatly increased in the past four years. The following table shows the annual increase rate:

1931 3% 1933 15%

1932 11% 1934 24%

If commercial transactions now account for one-quarter of commercial circulation, then industrial products should account for one-third of commercial transactions. Commercial transactions are now of great significance for normal supply."

Secondly, the increase in grain sources (production) has led to a reduction in grain prices in recent years, which is also of great significance for abolishing the bread rationing system. In Moscow, comparing September 1934 with September 1933, the rate of decline in grain prices is shown in the following table:

Rye bread 37% Wheat flour 47%

Rye flour 33% Millet 44%

Wheat bread 25%

According to statistics from 1930, the increase in products from collective farms has increased to about 75% of the imports into 28 large cities. From this, it can be seen that the increase in grain has a great impact on the abolition of the bread rationing system. Moreover, due to the strengthening of trade in collective farms and the development of state commerce, the Party and the government considered that the adjustment of commercial rice should improve commerce, and should not reduce its role. Therefore, in the summer of 1934, the Soviet government, according to Stalin's suggestion, organized the Internal Trade Committee to strengthen the development of trade. This also has a great relationship with the abolition of the bread rationing system.

The implementation of the bread rationing system was to ensure the industrial development and rural economic transformation of the Soviet Union, and its abolition was due to the large increase in grain production and the transition to the development of grain trade.

In his report, Molotov finally clearly stated the significance of abolishing the bread rationing system, saying: "The significance of abolishing the bread rationing system lies in continuing to improve the supply to cities and villages, and further meet the needs of the people. Replacing bread rations with grain trade is a sign of the development of the Soviet Union, the change in the rural economy, and the victory of socialized eating. Because we are stronger than before, we have abolished the bread rationing system. This decision is of great significance to the national economy, not only enough to improve the supply to the people, but also enough to intensify political consolidation. In addition, it can develop Soviet commerce and consolidate the price of the ruble. The abolition of the bread rationing system indicates that the main task of the Second Five-Year Plan has been completed; after that, it will be how to develop trade and abolish the bread rationing system."

In November, after the Soviet government decided to abolish the bread rationing system, it began to implement it on January 1, 1935.

According to the estimates of the Soviet authorities, at least 120 million poods of wheat can be stored in 1935 to maintain the grain supply until the new wheat is on the market. Moreover, there is still a lot of grain left over from previous stores, which can be enough to supply the market. According to the statistics of the State Harvest Committee, the harvest in 1934 was the same as the previous year, and because of the improvement in harvest technology, 250 million to 300 million poods more could be harvested. Therefore, the implementation of the abolition of the bread rationing system can be effectively guaranteed.

After the abolition of the bread rationing system, the state must first set the price of bread and increase the wages of workers. At the same time, increase the production of cooperative bread, especially to increase the production and development of bread in areas where bread production is lagging behind. Because the change in the price of bread and flour will affect the price of general food, especially if the price of wheat is too low, it is easy to promote speculation and waste wheat. Therefore, the government must curb and consider this dangerous tendency.

At the same time, because the price of bread has increased slightly due to the abolition of bread coupons, the wages of workers must also be increased accordingly to adapt to this new living condition. And pay the workers in cash to facilitate the application of the market and stabilize the value of the Soviet currency - the ruble.

Due to the stability of the ruble price, commodity prices have also fallen, which is a great improvement in the lives of the Soviet people. On November 15, 1935, the Soviet government further unified the standards of commodity prices, abolished the state-owned store system and reformed the currency system to adapt domestic trade to foreign trade. This increased the convenience of purchasing for the general public. Moreover, because of the reduction in commodity prices, the wages of workers have been increased invisibly. According to the order of the Soviet government in September 1935, the bread coupon system was further abolished in October of this year, and it was completely abolished on January 1, 1936.

A TASS dispatch from Moscow on September 26 stated:

"...The Central Committee of the All-Union Communist Party and the People's Committee decided that from October 1, the prices of bread, flour, coarse and fine flour, grains, pasta, rice, and confectionery will be reduced across the board, and the quota rationing system for meat products, fats, sugar, and potatoes will be abolished. The State Cooperative will sell them to the people at the national unified prices in each region. The price reductions for various commodities in Moscow are as follows:

Bread reduced by 15%

Rye flour reduced by 24%

Wheat flour reduced by 14%

Coarse flour reduced by 4% to 13%

Rice reduced by 19%

Fish and meat reduced by 36% strongly

Granulated sugar reduced by 30%

Block reduced by 35%

Butter reduced by 31%

Artificial cheese reduced by 30%

Potatoes reduced by 14%

The prices of other commodities in other regions are reduced in proportion."

In addition, according to a TASS communication from Grozny on October 22, there are also records of the development of commerce in the Soviet Union after the abolition of the bread coupon system. The original text reads: "During the First and Second Five-Year Plans, the retail commerce of the Soviet Union increased more than sixfold. This year (1935), the domestic retail commerce has increased by 35%. At the same time, the prices of various important foods have also seen a rapid and systematic decline. In the past three months, there have been more than 30 kinds of price reductions. On October 1 this year, compared with the commodity prices in December last year, the price of bread was reduced to one-half, the price of sugar was reduced to one-third, and the price of rice and meat was reduced to two-thirds. The prices of butter, vegetable oil, and bacon were reduced to one-half. In the first half of this year, urban consumers saved 600 million rubles due to price reductions. The activation of commerce resulted in the complete abolition of various food coupons on October 1 this year. At present, hundreds of new food stores selling meat, fish, milk, and bread have been added in various cities and villages. The goods are abundant, and the Soviet food industry has exceeded its planned production by tens of millions of pounds this year. The annual plan for butter, cheese, and sausages has been completed. The Soviet Union's reduction of commodity prices has not only failed to weaken commerce, but has also made it prosper rapidly. In the first two weeks of October, the turnover in Moscow reached 425,005,000 rubles. The sales of butter and vegetable oil have increased by onefold, and meat, fish, and sugar have also increased greatly. State-owned and cooperative stores have abundant goods. Not only have food prices been reduced, but also the prices of fabrics, soap, tobacco, and other categories have also been reduced. In October, the average price of meat in various cities in the Soviet Union was reduced by 30% compared to September, and the average price of butter was reduced by 20%. Therefore, the resolution of the 17th National Congress of the Communist Party to reduce retail prices by 35% during the Second Five-Year Plan has been realized.

From the above telegrams, it seems that the progress of the Soviet Union's abolition of the bread coupon system has generally achieved great results. If it is compared with the famine in the initial chaotic state and the serious grain problem that is occurring, it is truly impossible to calculate. Although the Soviet Union's abolition of the bread coupon system today is not considered to have completely solved the grain problem, it has at least achieved a further expression, which is probably undoubted. On the contrary, if we look back at the current economic panic that is happening in the capitalist world (including colonies and semi-colonies), there is serious unemployment, famine, disasters, and wars everywhere... pushing the masses into the sea of death... it is truly incomparable.

Let us cite the recent "Political Daily" of Denmark, the "Prague Daily" of Czechoslovakia, and the Berlin communication in the "Truth Daily" of the Soviet Union, which reported on the real situation of the food panic in the "Third Reich" Germany under Hitler's rule, to make a clear comparison with the improvement of the current grain problem in the Soviet Union.

The Czech "Prague Daily" said on November 3: "In recent days, the lack of butter and other oils in Germany has been extremely acute. The queues in front of food stores are getting longer every day. People have to spend three hours to buy a quarter of a pound of butter, and sometimes they can't even buy it. General housewives are troubled and disappointed. Although they often stand in front of the stores, they still can't get the oil products necessary for their homes. Not only is there no butter, but also artificial cheese and lard will be gone. There is also a great lack of other foods."

The Soviet "Truth Daily" said on November 4: "Recently, the difficulty of food in Berlin has intensified, which shows the deterioration of the national economic situation in Germany. The lines in front of food stores have become a daily phenomenon. These lines are getting longer every day. The quantity of food that consumers can buy is decreasing very rapidly... Now butter, lard, pork, and other oils are sold according to the prescribed standards. Although the standards for the sale of butter, artificial cheese, and butter have not yet been prescribed, the prices of these foods have already soared, which is beyond the reach of the general public. In Germany, the cheapest and most popular food is pork. Recently, although the official has raised the price of meat and strictly prohibits further price increases, there is still an unusual shortage of pork. In the past few days, the price of meat has soared by 20%.

The Danish "Political Daily" also said on November 2: "The prices prescribed by the official are generally not observed. All foods in the city secretly raise prices. The prices of meat scraps consumed by the poor, which are not managed by the official, have soared by 60% within a few days. Although there is police interference in the queues in front of the stores, the voices of opposition are endless. Construction workers in enterprises in the northern part of Berlin have announced a strike, saying that their stomachs are very hungry and they have to separate to seek food."

If we analyze this comparison clearly, we can find the realistic factors that are inevitably reflected in the period of capitalist decline. However, this is not limited to the issue of grain. Therefore, the discussion of the grain problem in the Soviet Union should not be regarded as a simple problem, because it is closely related to the economic development in the Soviet Union. Sometimes, from the progress of the grain problem, we can even see the domestic political changes or stability. The current grain panic in the "Third Reich" is a good example. December 28, 1935

Preconditions for China's Grain Control 192

— Li Yinbei

The importance of the current food problem lies in the shortage of rice and grain. To preserve a sufficient amount of food for the people for regulation and control, the following conditions must first be met. New-style warehouses must be built. The current warehouses for storing rice and grain are mostly old-style grain warehouses or renovated rented houses. The rice and grain stored are mostly commercial goods, and due to financial conditions, they must be taken out of the warehouse and turned over in a few months. Therefore, in terms of storage equipment, there is no need for any special equipment. However, as Japan has a lot of rice and grain, it can be preserved for more than ten years. Then, its warehouse equipment is definitely not comparable to profit-making properties. Therefore, our country must, at the very least, ensure that some of the food can be preserved for several years without changing. The quantity of rice and grain stockpiled nationwide must be controlled. Because the current grain warehouses in various places and the rice and grain warehouses with commercial behavior are tools for middlemen to hoard and speculate on the food of the people. Whenever new grain is harvested, they use low prices to purchase rice in large quantities from farmers, stockpile it in warehouses, and wait for a good price to sell it. If this kind of behavior is not controlled, it will also affect the future of the food of the people. Therefore, the volume of existing warehouses in each place should be registered first, and then the needs of a certain place should be verified, and the number of commercial operations should be allocated. If there are surplus warehouses, they should be leased or purchased by the government. The processing industry of food nationwide must be registered. Rice has a short storage period, while grain has a long storage period. Therefore, grain cannot be stored for a long time after it is ground into rice. Therefore, the third condition for preserving the food of the people is to pay attention to the problem of grinding grain. At present, the grinding of grain by the people is mostly unrestricted. They only want the mill to keep turning, regardless of the consumption of grain. In order to preserve the food of the people, the grain mill industry nationwide should be registered first so that restrictions can be imposed when necessary.

Secondly, it must be resolved from the following five aspects:

(A) Cultivated Land Area (Note 1)

The Stock Market Before the Unified Bond Issue 196

Last week (January 27th to February 1st), the Chinese Merchants Securities Exchange was preparing for the start of March futures trading, following the January futures delivery, and it was also the start of the Lunar New Year red market. Due to various factors, it experienced unprecedented changes. Trading only occurred on two of the six days. Monday was the last day of closure, and Thursday and Friday were for delivery. Saturday saw an effective halt. The surge and plunge in market prices caused considerable volatility. The fundamental reason for this was entirely due to the interest rate reduction and postponement. Amidst this ambiguous situation, large investors were heavily engaged in speculation. The Ministry of Finance then ordered a thorough investigation and restricted short sellers, requiring them to submit the actual goods. They were also required to cover previous short positions with the actual goods. Yesterday's report mentioned the Ministry of Finance's decision to issue 146 million in unified public bonds, divided into five types: A, B, C, D, and E, to recall all previously issued bonds and issue 34 million in Reconstruction Bonds for exchange within a four-month period starting from February 1st. The Exchange will likely face various disputes and difficulties when handling the February futures delivery. It is expected that the authorities will have remedial measures. Regarding last week's events, Tuesday's red market was also the last day of January futures trading. It briefly rose but then fell sharply. The January six contract experienced a severe limit down. On Wednesday, only the March futures contract was traded. Due to the requirement of submitting the actual goods, retail investors covered their short positions, causing a sharp rise of several jiao to as much as 3.6 yuan. Thursday and Friday were market closures for January futures delivery. Saturday encountered extreme difficulties and failed to open. The March futures contract therefore failed to begin trading. Yinbian rice was flat and sluggish. Market prices: White japonica high-grade was assessed, with medium and lower grades increasing by a few fen. Tomb of the Unknown Hero 205

During the Shanghai Incident in the 21st year of the Republic (1932), our army fought bitterly for over thirty days. Among them, the battle of Miaohangzhen was the longest and suffered the most casualties. The remains of the martyred generals have been buried at the foot of Zijin Mountain. For the remaining soldiers and the civilians who died in the disaster, it was proposed at the time to build a Tomb of the Unknown Hero in the southeast corner of the town. I once wrote a long poem in mourning. The years have passed, and five years have passed. Recently, the tomb has been completed. Therefore, I re-examined the old manuscript and wrote it for the gods, and I hope to cry together with all the caring people in the country. (Hu Junfu)

The road is winding and the car is far away, the clouds are dissolving and the sky is high. My heart is annoyed by injustice and my words are clumsy, my tears are about to run dry and my eyes are scorched. I would rather mutter to the wall in a dream than shout in vain in distress. Spring river moon, autumn river tide, a wine flag one foot lightly waving. Three or five village houses are not trimmed with thatch. Don't dislike the light taste, pour turbid wine. I will invite butchers and wine sellers to play. You strike the building block and I play the panpipes. Gentlemen and ladies offer flowers and sing. Broken rivers and mountains are a burden to bear. It is rare to come to the world once. You are all good brothers, I am distressed by the extinction of my essence. There are few bones and a desolate soul here, as if I hear the wind and rain calling in the middle of the night, and like thunder and lightning in the empty dust. The tomb is inscribed with five characters, a stone of ten feet, which will compete with the peaks of the Himalayas. Standing upright and reaching the sky for thousands of generations, even a robbery fire cannot burn it. Moreover, flowers and bamboo bloom in all seasons, and the fragrance is intertwined. It is the residence of dragons and the nest of phoenixes. Gods come to play and travel, no children are allowed to pick firewood, wolves and leopards stay away and foxes escape. Alas! A gentleman's death is heavier than Mount Tai, or lighter than a feather. The weight of a feather and Mount Tai is the same, but pine and cypress wither later. Life is noble and lowly, death is equal, life is not free, death is free. The great events in the world are not yet finished, and the buried mounds cannot be poured. Suddenly a dream of a deer overturning a banana tree. Buddha said that becoming a Buddha is not a matter of one morning. Come back with a wish, the body is strong and firm. All sentient beings in the world are seeds of Buddha, sacrificing themselves to feed tigers is also heroic. Alas! Famous and nameless are trivial, but being able to produce heroes is not lonely. I want to whisper to the people in the tomb, but I am afraid that worldly eyes will not recognize and be ridiculed. Alas! Raising a pen is like a sword out of its sheath, truly laboring and worrying to write a portrait for you. Unless I die beside the tomb of Yao Li, burn the pen and inkstone and wield a big knife. Otherwise, bury the poem in the tomb of poetry, and also know that the Yangtze River flowing east cannot wash it away. The soul of poetry becomes an immortal and rides on the clouds with you. The Calendar's Broadcast 206

— Qing Qu

A "calendar" is, in a way, an inanimate object. However, throughout the 365 days of the year, it constantly changes its face for you to see. If you don't believe it, look! Right before your eyes, that thick stack of paper is coming to an end with only a few pages of days remaining. If it were truly dead, then: what is passing by like flying?

Therefore, the "calendar," though hanging on the wall or placed on the table, seems to tell us every day, from morning to night, not to easily miss out. Moreover, month after month, it never fails to indicate the designated days. And when it comes to the week, it very clearly presents itself before your eyes, teaching you that this day is for rest! However, it faithfully shows that each day has its own light. Some people, however, don't interact with the "calendar" day by day. For example, if the 20th is torn off, and then every five or six days, or even more than ten days later, one grabs a stack and tears them off, you think about it, living such a muddled life! The "calendar" has not failed you, but you have indeed offended the "calendar," you must admit it!

Therefore, the "calendar" cannot speak, but on the last day of the year, it really cannot help but shout, "What great things have you done this year? In the end, you only end up betraying the country, earning yourself a 'traitor' title, calling and running around, better than several thousand elementary school students!" Alas! The "calendar" truly seems extremely angry, vaguely shouting to all the people of China.

Little Western Paradise 207

— Written by Zhang Henshui

Chapter Twenty-Third: Arguing Earnestly Around the Room, Seizing the Opportunity to Sue; Pouring the Wine and Joining Forces, Forgetting Grievances for Profit

Wang Shicheng said, "Ten thousand yuan is not a small amount, but our piece of land is also not small." As he spoke, he touched his body and took out a cotton paper drawing, handing it to Jia Duocai to see. The size of the land on the drawing, and how the four boundaries were, were all written clearly. And a piece of land on the eastern boundary was written as the Tang family's land, totaling two acres and seven fen, which was exactly the piece of land that the bank had entrusted them to buy. According to the current land price, it is worth at least 17,000 or 18,000 yuan. And Jin Ziqiang is only giving people 10,000 yuan, including the section in Xianyang, which is a great bargain. So he nodded twice and said, "The goods are sold to those who know their value. According to your meaning, how much money do you want?" Wang Shicheng said, "It can't be considered my meaning, it can only be said to be the meaning of my clan. They want a total of 15,000 or 16,000." Jia Duocai smiled and said, "If you talk about bargaining, it can't be considered too much, but the goods are sold to those who love them. If the buyer wants them or doesn't want them, and doesn't think much of this piece of land, you still want to sell it for a high price, that is naturally impossible." Jin Ziqiang heard Jia Duocai say these words, which simply broke his deal, and he was naturally very unhappy in his heart. But he had welcomed him in very warmly, and now he couldn't just chase him out, so he took out the cigar he was holding in his mouth, slowly tapping it on the edge of the table, and looked at Jia Duocai and said, "If you say this, brother, this brother Wang will not sell it even more. It's not that I necessarily want to covet Mr. Wang's family property, but I think Mr. Wang's land is too large, and he wants to sell it together with that piece of land in Xianyang. May I ask, at a time when the train is still so far away, no matter what business you do, everyone has no certainty, who would be willing to spend a lot of money to buy a vacant lot and leave it idle here?" Wang Shicheng finished drinking that cup of tea, slowly put down the teacup, his face blank, as if thinking about something. Then he slowly stood up, smiled faintly, and said, "I'll take my leave first, we'll talk another day." After he finished speaking, he stood up again, and looked as if he was about to leave. Mai Duocai stretched out his hand and stopped him, and smiled, "The mountain doesn't turn, the road turns. Doing such a big business is not like buying vegetables at the fire door, where you can settle the deal with just a few words. If you don't sell it to Mr. Jin, is there no one else who wants it?" Another Pose of Xi Shi 208

— Lin Shen

Last autumn, the Hangzhou Authors Association, National Academy of Art, Southeast Daily, and China Cultural Construction Association jointly hosted a banquet for the Shanghai Theater teachers and students at the Jinghu Hall on the north shore of West Lake. At that time, the most noticeable thing for Hangzhou people was the handshake and photo of the Shanghai Xi Shi and the Hangzhou Xi Shi.

Coincidentally, the two Xi Shis have the same surname, Cheng, and they both have the same high nose bridge. Of course, the young woman who is generally recognized as being able to play Xi Shi has a considerable beauty, without the need for excessive adjectives such as "shutting the moon and shaming the flowers."

Cheng Jingzi, the so-called "Shanghai Xi Shi," has facial contours rich in Oriental colors. Therefore, according to some actors in the Shanghai Theater, when Chen Dabe was examining new students through the Vocational Education Society, he discovered this little girl with Xi Shi's appearance hiding in a corner. Later, after three months of training, this Ms. Cheng indeed showed her surpassing talent in various subjects such as vocal music, dance, and performance. However, because she was young, timid, and lacked social experience, during the rehearsal of the musical "Xi Shi," this Ms. Cheng was still uneasy and felt that she would not live up to the expectations of the public, and repeatedly politely declined Chen Dabe, who was in charge of directing. Dabe just smiled and ignored it. After "Xi Shi" returned with honors from four places in Beijing, Hangzhou, Suzhou, and Wuxi, Ms. Cheng has been noticed by people in both the film and theater industries. If the organizers of the Shanghai Theater had been someone else, this "Shanghai Xi Shi" would have turned into a whirlpool long ago, and who knows what jokes would have been made.

Yesterday, I visited "Candle Night" at the Carlton and saw a preview hanging on the wall of the hall, "The Shanghai Theater will perform Chocolate Girl this Sunday," with a small makeup photo of "Ms. Cheng Jingzi of Chocolate Girl" pasted in the middle. Oh dear! This is like a Western girl! Where is there even a trace of oriental color? The beauty Xi Shi of Wu and Yue has transformed into a Chocolate Girl who has captivated the people of Paris, and can do so without revealing a trace. The makeup skills are so miraculous, I can't help but admire Ms. Cheng's talent and the results of the Shanghai Theater's half-year training.

According to the ticket seller at the Carlton, the director of the play, Chen Dabe, also plays the important role of Chocolate King in the play (the father of Chocolate Girl), and it is not just an empty gimmick in the advertisement. Although the performance results are difficult to predict, judging from the "still photos" displayed at the Carlton, this performance must have a considerable contribution in terms of stage technology.

Seeking Plum Blossoms in the Snow 209

— Seen in Records — (Sun Choucheng)

Yesterday afternoon at one o'clock, passing through Laoxidou Heping Road, I saw more than a dozen people gathered at the entrance of the Xinhua Bank. Upon closer inspection, there was a boy of eleven or twelve years old, wearing a old and worn bean-paste-colored floral satin jacket, kneeling on the sidewalk, his brows furrowed and locked in sorrow, not saying a word. On the ground, the sixteen characters "Father unemployed, mother ill, suffering from hunger and cold, please help" were written in chalk, and there were more than ten silver dollars in front of his knees. Beside him was a young child of about three or four years old, sitting in a tattered cotton cushion, with tears streaming down his face, which was unbearable to witness. The audience was sighing at his pitifulness, and some were lamenting his cold. Just as they were reaching for money, a man and a woman passed by, arm in arm, and watched for a long time. The woman wanted to take money and give it to him, but the man suddenly stopped her and said, "This is a pretense of poverty, hoping for people to pity them, don't be fooled." And he led her away. The other spectators who were about to take money were stopped, and they all withdrew their hands and scattered like crows and beasts. The boy kneeling on the ground, seeing the spectators about to give him copper coins, but suddenly withholding them, could not help but burst into tears.

Talking About Law 212

— Tingfang

On a journey, I met a judge and casually chatted. He said that the cases he had handled could be summarized as being either for money or for lust!

Originally, in this vast world, how many people can escape the traps of money and lust?

However, knowledgeable people can restrain themselves. Speaking of nature, it can be said categorically that everyone is the same.

At the same time, we can know that the law is only a passive thing. The ancients made laws only as a last resort! It is best to use positive persuasion.

Moreover, the people's violation of the law has a close relationship with the social conditions. If the society is good, the number of people who break the law will naturally decrease. If the society is bad, the number of people who break the law will naturally increase. Only punishing crimes without trying to improve the bad society, its effect can be said to be equal to zero!

Ultimately, we bear this heavy burden to do the work of transforming society. Other issues can be put aside.

Living next door to me is a certain ×× incense shop. It is said that the old couple who opened this shop are a very superstitious old couple. Talking Points

"Using Barbarians to Control Barbarians" vs. "Using Chinese to Destroy Chinese" 216

— Xing An

Recently, our "friendly nations" have often expressed dissatisfaction with our country's adoption of the policy of "using barbarians to control barbarians," viewing it as antagonistic towards them. They claim this is a mistake by China and the cause of Sino-foreign hatred, urging China to quickly change its attitude, abandon other countries, and implement "friendly cooperation" with them to jointly advance East Asia towards prosperity. Officials are undoubtedly dissatisfied, constantly considering settling this matter with us. As for the people, there is also much dissatisfaction. Some time ago, a thinker from a "friendly nation" expressed this sentiment. In a letter to a certain Chinese scholar, he plainly stated: "Your country's policy of using barbarians to control barbarians, and its antagonism towards XX, is a well-known fact worldwide. The United States has helped your country in this way, and Britain has also cunningly dealt with XX. And what has Soviet Russia done for your country? How have your representatives advocated for alliance with Russia and accommodation of the Communists? These events are still vividly etched in our memories. And what were the results? We also remember that."

"Using barbarians to control barbarians" is a common international policy. When countries A and B are antagonistic, each often allies with one or two third parties to resist the other. Leaving aside other countries' situations, let's take our "friendly nation" as an example. The past "Anglo-Japanese Alliance" and the recently widely rumored "German-Japanese Alliance" are examples of this policy in action. As for China, the "using barbarians to control barbarians" policy may have been adopted, but it has not been beneficial to our country. We have only ever heard of conspiracies to divide us, and have never seen anyone willing to help our country control other countries. A certain Chinese scholar said it well: "Our country is not worthy of being friends with anyone, and even less worthy of being enemies with anyone. Because friendship is equality, and enmity is also equality."

In reality, the "using barbarians to control barbarians" policy is still fair. The "using Chinese to destroy Chinese" tactic is the truly insidious and terrifying one. Recently, our "friendly nation," while expressing dissatisfaction with our country's adoption of the "using barbarians to control barbarians" policy, is employing the "using Chinese to destroy Chinese" tactic. They personally reached out and seized the land of the four northeastern provinces. But to deceive the world, they created a "puppet state," driving a few Chinese traitors to act as their "running dogs." This is the "using Chinese to destroy Chinese" tactic. The rebellion in eastern Hebei and the establishment of the second "puppet organization" are also the result of the "friendly nation" using the "using Chinese to destroy Chinese" tactic. Furthermore, the North China autonomy movement, which was active for a while recently, is nothing more than a manifestation of this same tactic. In short, the current China policy adopted by our "friendly nation" is not "direct aggression" but "indirect aggression." They exhaust methods of "luring with benefits" and "coercion" to make Chinese traitors submit and betray their country. This tactic is extremely clever; it's a deadly scheme that kills without bloodshed. Unfortunately, some of our nation's madmen are willing to "act as accomplices for the tiger," truly great sinners of the nation. Therefore, we feel that while we must resist foreign insults, we must also eliminate traitors. Because those who will destroy China are not only "foreign enemies" but also "internal traitors."

The Old Boatman 217

— Xin Ye

The earth was panting, as if unable to withstand the pressure of the sub-zero temperatures.

The sky was frozen in a grey gloom; the northwest wind swept down from the peaks of the Dalongtou Mountains. The whole universe seemed to be immersed in a swimming kiln. The old boatman, A Gen, facing the cold wind and treading on the frozen snow, held the tow rope tightly on his shoulder, and walked along the long embankment of the Wujiu Pond.

He hunched over, pulling down the earflaps of his torn felt hat, while his hands were tucked into his sleeves. He walked step by step, sideways. There was no sound, no shadow, just the effort of pulling the tow rope and hurrying forward. The biting north wind blocked him, forcing him to straighten up and take a breath every few steps.

The harbor water was flowing against the current, and the wind was also blowing against him. The broken little boat slowly drifted on the water three or four feet from the shore, the tow rope bending the short mast into a bow shape. His wife sat on the stern, carefully steering the rudder.

It was already dusk. A few crows returning to their nests in the bare branches of the sparse forest cawed, "Yah! Yah! Yah!" spreading their desolate and melancholic tones into the frozen air.

The earth was grey, the sky was grey, and the old boatman A Gen's mood was also grey.

The small broken boat was loaded with firewood, which he was taking to the town of Shihutou. The small boat was already very old, and now, loaded with dozens of bundles of firewood, the footboards were almost submerged in the water. Water had seeped in through several cracks. The boat was moving exceptionally slowly, like a snail. If the old boatman A Gen stopped even for a moment, it would start to drift backward.

The sound of water lapping under the boat was like a soft sigh. The wind blew against the rope on the bare mast, making a monotonous flapping sound. The surrounding air was stagnant, and the river was quiet. He rarely encountered any passing boats, only occasionally a small, fast inland river steamer cutting through the water and speeding past, causing waves to crash against the embankment, its long, wailing horn echoing through the frozen air. At the same time, the small broken boat shuddered violently, almost pulling the old boatman A Gen off the embankment.

The old boatman A Gen hated the small steamer the most, because it was his life's enemy. Before the fast boat service started on this harbor, his small broken boat was the only small ship carrying passengers and goods on this harbor. He used to make one trip every day, going up one day and down the next, from Shuijing to Shihutou Town, earning at least four or five thousand coins a day. Back then, he even employed three crew members on his boat. Every year around June or July, the small boat would have to be taken ashore for repairs or caulking. For half his life, he had relied on this small boat. Although he hadn't accumulated much extra, he had cleared the debts he owed when his parents died and the expenses of his own wedding. Back then, his wife stayed at home taking care of the children, while he entrusted all the work on the boat to the captain, Ma Zi Er. As soon as the boat set off, he would sit alone on the flat stone surface in the fire cabin, smoking or drinking liquor. But since the fast inland river service started, his livelihood had been suddenly cut off. Moreover, recently there had been more bandits on the river, so shopkeepers were afraid to entrust goods to him, and passengers preferred to take the steamer. Now, he could only make a meager living by carrying firewood or vegetables for others.

He walked along, thinking, the mud under his feet frozen as hard as stone. The wind howled fiercely, and the earth seemed to be on its last breath. Tragic colors and a sorrowful atmosphere wove a curtain that blurred before his eyes.

The sky gradually darkened, and the trees and paths became blurred outlines. Only the sound of the ruthless northwest wind was so loud that it seemed to be uprooting the bare trees. The outside of the old boatman A Gen's body was as cold as ice, but his heart was burning with anxiety. He was both anxious and afraid, but he couldn't walk any faster.

It was still about seven li from Shihutou Town, but it was already dark. He had to wipe his running nose with his hand, use his hem to wipe the cold sweat from his forehead, and stop to gather the tow rope:

"Light the lamp, we can't tow anymore, let's row!" he said to his wife on the shore.

New Street Square 218

— Cong Long

—One of Impressions of the South Seas—

Everyone knows that Malaya, in the South Seas archipelago, is one of the world's richest tin-producing regions. New Street Square is indeed a famous tin-producing area in Malaya, a giant!

The distance from Kuala Lumpur to New Street Square is nine miles. By train, it costs only two cents to go back and forth. If you want comfort and speed, taking a public bus will only cost you eight cents more.

On a sunny day after a rain, I finally carved out half a day to visit the tin area - New Street Square - for a half-day trip. As I rode on the lightning-fast public bus, feeling the cool breeze on my face, the melancholy hidden in my heart was blown away. I deeply felt: Even the tropical South Seas have this refreshing weather!

The bus left the city area of Kuala Lumpur, gliding lightly through the fields like smoke. Along the way, we passed through villages. Massive iron factories stood tall along the roadside, booming loudly. Piles of atap houses crouched low in the fields, like wild beasts, seemingly afraid of escaping from the booming sounds of the iron factory. The road became increasingly uneven, and the speed of the bus decreased.

Upon arriving at New Street Square, whether on high mountains or flat ground, looking all around, chimneys stood in forests, like a burnt forest, the burnt remains standing as charcoal-black pillars on the open hillsides. Smoke billowed from the chimney openings, rippling in the air. Tin wells were everywhere, like many holes left after being washed by rain. The engines started one after another, echoing each other with incessant booms in the ears. Besides this, New Street Square had no other ancient monuments, scenic spots, or cool places for people to admire, stroll, or linger.

However, almost 90 percent of the residents here are our overseas Chinese compatriots. The largest tin wells also belong to our overseas Chinese compatriots.

Along the steep muddy road, we walked slowly past the public banana plantation and the sand embankment before taking a shortcut to the wells to see the tin mines.

When I arrived at the tin well, the sun was already setting. In the open sky, layers of deep grey velvet clouds rippled, seemingly a sign of rain. However, from time to time, a ray of sunlight shone through the gaps in the clouds. While panting, I kept taking out the handkerchief in my pocket to wipe the sweat from my forehead, climbing towards the tin well with an unsteady gait. When I reached a place where I could stand, I leaned forward to look into the magnificent project inside the tin well. Countless winding iron rails and heavy water pumps were working with rattling booms, mixed with the "ai-he" sounds of the workers, interweaving into a rhythmic song playing in the workshop.

I continued to climb upward, laboriously climbing to the tin-sifting bed, the highest point in the tin well. The spring water in the tin well all converged here, and the water flowed like a waterfall, rustling. Then, the tin sand was scooped up by countless tin-sifting workers from one ditch after another.

Seeing that the sun was about to kiss the mountains, the evening clouds embraced the orange-yellow sunset. The surrounding scenery was enveloped in smoke and clouds, presenting a dim color.

The magnificent tin well project and the spectacle of the sunset in the smoke and clouds were the deeply etched impressions of my half-day trip to New Street Square, which are still clearly etched in my mind.

Special Article

A Record of Visiting the Chiba Soy Sauce Business in Japan (2) 219

— (Ye Xiyuan)

From the Tang Dynasty until now, China and Japan have been manufacturing soy sauce using nearly the same original techniques. With the Meiji Restoration, the Industrial Revolution of Western Europe was also brought to Japan. The use of machinery fundamentally transformed production methods. Soy sauce, which had always been a special product of East Asian handicrafts, now had people attempting to mechanize its production. Recently, Japanese industry has advanced by leaps and bounds in everything. Even soy sauce, which had always been a handicraft, has emerged in Japan as a large-scale, mechanized production. Meanwhile, our soy sauce industry remains stuck in the primitive handicraft era, causing endless sighs of despair. Soy sauce can be said to be a uniquely East Asian product. Applying Western technology to the unique products of East Asia has allowed it to break free from the primitive handicraft era and become a large-scale modern enterprise. On this point, we cannot help but admire the Japanese for their extraordinary spirit and perseverance. To understand their business in order to lay the groundwork for the modernization of our country's soy sauce industry, the author traveled to Japan in 1931 to observe their achievements. However, since returning from Japan until now, three or four years have passed quickly. During this time, relations between China and Japan have been constantly uncertain, and our country's economic vitality has been declining. The hopes of the past remain just hopes, with no day in sight for their realization. When I recall the ambitions I had when I set out and pick up my pen to write this article, how can my heart not be filled with endless sadness?

Japan's soy sauce industry is mostly concentrated in three areas. One is the Kanto Chiba area, another is the Kansai Wakayama area, and the other is the Kyushu Fukuoka area. Some are famous for producing so-called light soy sauce, such as "Tatsuno" in Kansai. Some are famous for producing soy sauce using the so-called "fast brewing" method, such as "Nihon Jozo" in Tokyo. However, the largest companies with the widest sales are mostly in Chiba. Historically, Chiba has also been the most developed area for the soy sauce industry in Japan. This may be because Chiba's climate and water are particularly suitable for making soy sauce, or it may be because it is close to Edo (Tokyo), and word spread due to the propagation by high officials and nobles. Perhaps because the Shogunate was in Edo, Chiba's soy sauce industry developed as a result. In any case, judging from the overall situation of the soy sauce industry in Japan, the development of Chiba's soy sauce industry was relatively late. Because if the soy sauce making techniques were passed down from China, they would naturally have first developed in Kyushu and the Kansai area.

Song Introductions 220

Returning to My Hometown

Letters from home arrive piece by piece, long letters, scattered and messy, disorganized, covering the desk, making me anxious and clueless, without any idea what to do. In a foreign land; confused, drunk and lost in the entertainment district, living it up, where would I think of my hometown! Dazed, shrouded in a love net, unable to control myself, drunk and dying in a foreign land, where would I think of my old parents! Bewitching girls, fickle, I advise you not to take them to heart, don't linger, don't be sad, quickly pack your bags, prepare to leave this foreign land, return to your hometown, return to your hometown, return to your hometown.

Heroes are short of breath, children are long on emotion, we are all flesh and blood, we all have hearts, everyone cares about each other's joys and sorrows, why are we living in the same world, but our joys and sorrows are different? Pity me; lonely, wandering in a foreign land, in darkness, who knows my hometown! A scorched earth, not a blade of grass grows, family broken and dead, how to comfort my heart, pity those old parents of mine! Modern misses, unthinkable, I advise you not to bother, don't be lost in thought, don't daydream, quickly pack your bags, prepare to leave this foreign land, return to your hometown, return to your hometown, return to your hometown.

Suzhou Ballad 223

Cheng Fangzhou Li Liansun Mao Jiashu

Hua Mei (1060) 1:00 PM to 1:30 PM

Opening "Old New Year"

The wax plum's fragrance permeates the wax bottle anew. Poetic and artistic sentiments bind my heart. I drink pepper wine alone, pitying my white hair. Hurriedly writing auspicious Spring phrases, I recall red makeup. New Year's Day greetings urge poetic inspiration. Planning feasts and discussions of paintings keep us busy on the Lantern Festival. The world is peaceful, the common people are joyful. The New Year adds years and brings surplus wealth. Gambling games delight the ladies. Drinking games make the guests wild. How long ago did the winds and clouds change? What annoys people most is the damage to national defense. The decline of commerce brings worries about livelihood. The people are displaced by the chaos and panic. Hot blood has been exchanged for a new year. Cold-heartedness is worse than the old writings. I wish the New Year would bring a new national spirit. Let us stake our lives to do our part. Enduring hardship and toil in commerce and industry.

Xu Yunzhi's Three Smiles 224

Dong Lu (640) 2:30 PM to 3:30 PM

Opening "Plum Blossom"

Although the plum blossom is not the king of flowers. Its character is pure and lofty, surpassing all others. Since ancient times, poets have praised it. Its reputation as the flower champion is unmatched in the world. The chrysanthemum is the recluse among flowers. The lotus is also regarded as a gentleman. Zhou Zi loved the lotus, Tao loved the chrysanthemum. The two men's ideals were not ordinary. Little do they know. The plum is both a recluse and a gentleman. Its nature is gentle, its character is high, and its appearance is dignified. The world often praises peach and plum blossoms. Peach blossoms are enchanting, and plum blossoms are fragrant. That plum blossom. Only settles for the ordinary. Unwilling to follow the fashion and learn new makeup. It has a unique charm and is not vulgar. Ashamed to compete with peach and plum blossoms. Without a good matchmaker. What harm is there? The fairy of Miaogu originally had no groom. Her friends in the mountains are pine and bamboo. At night, there is a gentle breeze and the moon and frost. Those ordinary flowers can only listen to orders. Who can be the first to welcome the spring? Therefore, it is said that. The new moon stretches its eyebrows, and the stars shine. When the old plum opens its mouth, all the flowers are busy. Who knows it after heaven and earth grow old? They only say that the world is blind. But unexpectedly. The affectionate person is still Lin Hejing. The confidant must speak of Meng Xiang's intestines. Now, the determination of the national flower is even more glorious.

Du Wenkui's Red Robe

Zhong Xi (1040) 11:00 to 11:30

Opening "Lamenting the Dead"

The thatched cottage is desolate, beside the bamboo fence. The west wind is bleak, and the rain is drizzling. A few yellow chrysanthemums are just beginning to bloom. Touching the scenery breaks my heart with the most tragic feelings. Thinking of that. Last winter, my wife died of illness. Counting today, it has been more than half a year. During her lifetime, she loved the chrysanthemums by the fence the most. She cultivated them herself and never left them. Until now. The chrysanthemums are still there, but where is the person? Seeing the flowers, how can I not think of my late wife. Since coming to my home, she has followed the ways of a woman. Her needlework was never low. She always kept the courtyard clean. Her cooking was always delicious. When guests arrived, tea was always available. She used a lot of rue and Wuyi tea. She embroidered new patterns. She shook the cotton yarn spinning machine. She had silk and satin in her chests and boxes. She had prepared skirts and shirts for all seasons. She never dared to be greedy for sleep in the evening. She often read books on female precepts under the lamp. She saved silver to help me. She exchanged gold for treasures, and there was still more left over. She was filial to my parents. She quietly raised the children. In the hot summer, she drove away the mosquitoes with mosquito nets. When it was cool in autumn, she had to prepare winter clothes. Husband and wife lived together in harmony for many years. There was never any conflict or disagreement. Until now, the boudoir is empty, leaving only a portrait. Her soul is drifting, returning to the West.

Page 21

My parents' endless thoughts are mixed with tears. Examining my lowly self. My children are crying. Who will wipe the tables and chairs? Dust flies in my face. I sleep alone in a lonely coat, watching the remaining drips. The makeup table is desolate, the shadow is rare. I want to remarry a virtuous and capable woman. How can I, lamentably, lack money to move. Many feelings of love are hard to cut off. The road separates yin and yang, and there is no meeting date. Clearly, the mirror is split. Good birds nest in the same forest in two places. Who can I tell my bitter situation to?

Aftersound

The Asia Sound Harmonica Society is a newly emerging harmonica music group in Shanghai. The society is entirely organized by amateur comrades, aiming to popularize harmonica music, unlike those that aim to make a profit. It has been broadcasted on major radio stations many times and has been warmly welcomed by all walks of life. Now, in order to implement its original intention, the society is publicly soliciting the first session of new free comrades, beginner and advanced class leaders. In addition to waiving all membership fees and tuition fees, it also gives away exquisite lecture notes and sheet music. Ladies and gentlemen from all walks of life who love the harmonica, don't miss this good opportunity. The society has scheduled to open class leaders on February 9 (Sunday). The venue is at Room 311, 3rd Floor, Dahua Building, Nanjing Road and Zhejiang Road Intersection, Oriental Japanese School. The number of places is limited, so please hurry to register and request chapters.

The Thunder and Lightning Drama Society was scheduled to broadcast a special program at the Tongle Radio Station a few days ago. However, because the female lead had not yet returned to Shanghai, it was postponed to yesterday (2nd) and broadcasted the drama "Buying and Selling" at Li Shude Hall.

Dai Ping of the Datong Society also has the nickname "Big Boss."

According to Yu Jialin, the Song Star Pictorial is running out of advertisements and cannot support itself, so it has decided to cease publication after the fifth issue. (Above by Fengyi)

Miss Li Huijuan has joined the Yiguang Society drama group as the lead role in "Flower Girl."

The Jiujiu Society is rehearsing the drama "Uncle Liu San" recently.

The Shidai Society has been revived and renamed the Shidai Opera Society. (Above by Wang Zhifang)

The preparation work for the public performance of the Chong Sheng Society is extremely tense. It is heard that the society, in view of the fact that most of its female members are not fluent in Mandarin, is conducting Mandarin instruction class leaders, stipulating time to teach Mandarin, and continuing to solicit female members. A brochure will be sent upon request by letter.

After the reorganization of Lili Radio Station, Ni Gaofeng took over. Unexpectedly, on the first day, there was a sudden accident in the machine room, and all the machines were destroyed. They are currently being repaired. (Above by Yu Yun)

Miss Xu Xuan of the Lanman Art Society published the plot of her drama "Lost Home" in the "Xuefeng" column of the Dahua Daily.

The Peilei Opera Society and the Paris Art Society have already collaborated.

The Guotai Troupe broadcast on the City Music Station, and the gentlemen who came to visit were not as crowded as they were on the mainland.

Mr. Qiu Tiying has resigned from the Huamei Radio Station. (Above by Wang Liu)

Miss Xiao Dating Liying has been living a secluded life recently in order to restore her reputation. (Jiliu)

The Xinhua Society, "Returning from Glory with Han Zai," will start performing from yesterday (2nd) at the pier to Songjiang, performing at the Songjiang Grand Theater. The program includes "The Women's Army"...etc. (Jinlang)

Mr. Wang Fuchang, formerly of the Metropolitan, has spare power to reorganize his troops.

After moving to its new location, the Peilei Vocal Music Society is continuing to recruit male and female members. The address is Fangxie Road or Xinxin Radio Station on Nanjing Road.

The Midnight Music Society is also currently at a standstill.

"The Good Earth" Leading Actor 227

There is a Wang Long in Beiping

MGM filmed "The Good Earth." Its director once came to China. In Beiping, they found a male lead, also named Wang Long, who is from Hebei, graduated from Yenching University, his father is an engineer, and he has been running an engineering business in Shanghai for more than ten years. His mother is American and now teaches in Tianjin. According to Wang Long himself, MGM wanted him to go to the United States, but his father did not allow it. He plans to come to Shanghai within the month to try out for the film industry and hopes to serve the Chinese film industry. (National)

A Battle Scene in "Battlefield Heroes" 228

— Grand Cathay Theatre

"Rouge Tiger" Has Been Sent to Beijing 229

Wang Cilong has joined Yihua as a guest director for "Rouge Tiger," which is a detective-style patriotic drama. In addition to the leading actors Hu Ping, Wang Yin, Wang Naidong, Zhang Zhizhi, etc., he himself also plays a role. The preliminary script was sent to Beijing a few days ago and filming is expected to begin in mid-month. At the same time, Hu Ping is expected to return to work soon.

"Avatar Girl" Working Intensely 230

"Avatar Girl," starring Yuan Meiyun, Wang Yin, Xu Manli, Ye Wenqiu, Han Langan, Qin Tong, Jiang Xiu, Wang Guilin, etc., and directed by Fang Peilin, has been working very hard since filming began. In recent days, they have been rushing to shoot several scenes with a Nanyang background, and it is said that the results are very satisfactory.

"A Flower" Begins Filming 231

"A Flower," directed by Xu Suling, which has a dance troupe as its background, has already passed the preliminary script review, and the second script review has also been sent to Beijing. It is expected to start filming in mid-month. This play depicts the rise and fall of a dancer, as well as the changes in the social environment. The theme of the play is said to be very sad and beautiful.
